# Run 20260607T070653Z-82693

- goal source: .dev/goals/261-permission-pipeline-extraction.md
- goal tag:    permission-pipeline-extraction
- provider:    minimax
- model:       MiniMax-M3
- baseline:    91357cd

## Goal

```
# Goal 261 ÔÇö Extract `PermissionPipeline` from `ToolRegistry::invoke_with_audit` (R-1)

**Roadmap**: Code quality ÔÇö architecture review follow-up (P1 backlog)

**Design principle check**:
- Implemented as: new struct `PermissionPipeline` in a sibling module, called from
  `invoke_with_audit` (which becomes a thin dispatch wrapper)
- ÔØî Does NOT branch inside `agent.rs::Agent::run`'s main loop
- ÔØî Does NOT change the public API of `ToolRegistry` (existing callers continue
  to work; the pipeline is an internal refactor)

## Why

Architecture review (`docs/review/architecture-review-2026-06-07.md`,
items R-1, H-4) flagged that `ToolRegistry::invoke_with_audit` at
`src/tools/mod.rs:735-1016` is a 281-line god-method that mixes six
concerns in a single function:

1. **Auto-classifier check** (LLM-based, 32 lines, 745-784) ÔÇö delegates
   to a separate classifier when `PermissionMode::Auto`
2. **Static permission check** (rules + Strict mode, 30 lines, 786-816)
3. **Permission-hook check** for non-headless interactive tools
   (57 lines, 818-874)
4. **External-hook dispatch** for headless interactive tools
   (40 lines, 876-915)
5. **L1 policy check** (shell + fs sandbox, 28 lines, 945-972)
6. **Tool dispatch + audit metadata** (40 lines, 974-1015)

Stages 1-5 are all permission-related; only stage 6 is "actually run the
tool." The current shape has these problems:

- **Each stage is hidden behind a single function call** ÔÇö to test the
  policy path, you have to drive a full `ToolRegistry` and walk
  through 200 lines of irrelevant setup.
- **`ToolRegistry` is 14 fields of policy + I/O + observability** ÔÇö
  see the struct at `src/tools/mod.rs:287-321` (already called out as
  H-4 in the review).
- **The Transform variant of `PermissionDecision`** (line 837) mutates
  the arguments in place and silently continues; this is hard to spot
  in the middle of 200 lines.
- **`unwrap_or_else` at line 756** is the only `unwrap` in the
  function ÔÇö extraction will let us push it to a typed error path.

The goal: pull stages 1-5 into a new struct `PermissionPipeline` with
one method `check(name, args)`. `invoke_with_audit` becomes a thin
wrapper that calls `pipeline.check(...)?.await?` then dispatches the
tool. Each stage is independently testable. `tools/mod.rs` shrinks by
~200-300 lines.

## Scope (do exactly this, no more)

### 1. New file `src/tools/permission_pipeline.rs` ÔÇö define `PermissionPipeline`

Create a new module. Re-export it from `src/tools/mod.rs` (or
`src/tools/mod.rs` re-exports the public types only). Suggested shape:

```rust
//! Permission pipeline extracted from `ToolRegistry::invoke_with_audit`.
//! See `docs/review/architecture-review-2026-06-07.md` item R-1.

use std::sync::Arc;
use serde_json::Value;
use crate::agent::types::PermissionDecision;
use crate::error::Error;
use crate::hooks::ExternalHookRunner;
use crate::permissions::{PermissionMode, SharedPermissions};
use crate::policy_sandbox;
use crate::tools::auto_classifier::AutoClassifier;

#[derive(Clone)]
pub struct PermissionPipeline {
    /// Optional shared permissions lock (None = all allowed, backward
    /// compatibility for callers that don't configure permissions).
    pub permissions: Option<SharedPermissions>,
    /// Cached default permission mode (mirrors `PermissionsConfig.mode`).
    pub permission_mode: PermissionMode,
    /// Optional user-installed `PermissionHook` for non-headless callers.
    pub permission_hook: Option<Arc<dyn crate::permissions::PermissionHook>>,
    /// Optional L1 policy config (shell + fs sandbox).
    pub policy: Option<policy_sandbox::PolicyConfig>,
    /// Headless mode ÔÇö interactive tools go through external hooks.
    pub headless: bool,
    /// External hook runner for headless permission checks.
    pub hook_runner: ExternalHookRunner,
    /// Optional auto classifier for `PermissionMode::Auto`.
    pub auto_classifier: Option<Arc<tokio::sync::Mutex<AutoClassifier>>>,
}

impl PermissionPipeline {
    /// Construct a default (no-permissions) pipeline. Equivalent to the
    /// pre-Goal-197 behavior where all tools are allowed.
    pub fn permissive() -> Self { ... }

    /// Run all permission stages. On `Ok(())` the caller may proceed to
    /// dispatch the tool. On `Err(_)` the tool call must be denied with
    /// the returned error.
    ///
    /// `arguments` may be mutated in place when a `PermissionHook`
    /// returns `PermissionDecision::Transform`.
    pub async fn check(&self, name: &str, arguments: &mut Value) -> Result<(), Error> {
        // Stages 1-5 from the current `invoke_with_audit`, in order.
    }
}
```

**Important**: the body of `check` is a *move* of the existing code
from lines 736-931 (the Auto / static / Strict / hook / headless-hook
chain) plus lines 945-972 (the L1 policy check). Do not rewrite the
logic; preserve the exact behavior. The only allowed micro-changes:

- Replace `serde_json::to_string(&arguments).unwrap_or_else(|_| "{}".into())`
  (line 756) with a typed fallback that uses `tracing::warn!` instead
  of swallowing the error silently. (Optional, small.)
- Rename local variables to avoid shadowing `name` if it conflicts.

### 2. `src/tools/mod.rs` ÔÇö move fields, replace logic

**Step 2a: remove permission fields from `ToolRegistry`.**

Delete these fields from the struct (lines 297, 300, 305, 309, 312, 314, 320):

- `permissions: Option<SharedPermissions>`
- `permission_mode: PermissionMode`
- `permission_hook: Option<Arc<dyn PermissionHook>>`
- `policy: Option<policy_sandbox::PolicyConfig>`
- `pub headless: bool`
- `pub hook_runner: crate::hooks::ExternalHookRunner`
- `pub auto_classifier: Option<Arc<tokio::sync::Mutex<AutoClassifier>>>`

Keep the *other* fields: `tools`, `aliases`, `transport`, `touched`.

Add a new field:

```rust
/// Goal-261: extracted permission pipeline. Built by the registry
/// constructor; the registry no longer owns permission/policy/hook
/// fields directly.
permission_pipeline: PermissionPipeline,
```

**Step 2b: builder + setter plumbing.**

`ToolRegistryBuilder` (search for it in the same file) currently has
`permissions`, `permission_mode`, `permission_hook`, `policy`,
`headless`, `hook_runner`, `auto_classifier` setters. Change the
constructor to build a `PermissionPipeline` from those setters and
store it in `permission_pipeline`. The public setters can stay on the
builder (setters mutate the pipeline inside the builder) OR be removed
and replaced with a `with_pipeline(pipeline: PermissionPipeline)`
shortcut. **Pick the smaller diff**: keep the setters, change the
builder to accumulate the pipeline internally.

**Step 2c: rewrite `invoke_with_audit`.**

Replace the body of `invoke_with_audit` (lines 735-1016) with:

```rust
pub async fn invoke_with_audit(&self, name: &str, mut arguments: Value) -> ToolDispatch {
    // Stage 1-5: permission pipeline. Returns Err on any denial.
    if let Err(e) = self.permission_pipeline.check(name, &mut arguments).await {
        return ToolDispatch {
            result: Err(e),
            audit: AuditMeta::synthetic_unknown_tool(name),
        };
    }

    // Stage 6a: record touched files (observability, not permission).
    if let Some(slot) = &self.touched {
        record_touched(name, &arguments, slot);
    }

    // Stage 6b: tool lookup.
    let Some(tool) = self.find_by_name(name) else {
        return ToolDispatch {
            result: Err(Error::UnknownTool(name.into())),
            audit: AuditMeta::synthetic_unknown_tool(name),
        };
    };

    // Stage 6c: execute + audit.
    let side_effect = tool.side_effect_class();
    let step_id = uuid::Uuid::now_v7().hyphenated().to_string();
    let args_hash = blake3_canonical_json(&arguments);
    let started_at = unix_millis();
    let args_size = arguments.to_string().len();
    let span = tracing::info_span!("tool.execute", name = %name, args_size);
    let raw_result = tool
        .execute(arguments)
        .instrument(span)
        .await
        .map_err(|e| match e {
            Error::Tool { .. } | Error::BadToolArgs { .. } | Error::UnknownTool(_) => e,
            other => Error::Tool {
                name: name.into(),
                message: other.to_string(),
            },
        });

    let finished_at = unix_millis();
    let exit_status = match &raw_result {
        Ok(_) => ExitStatus::Ok,
        Err(e) => {
            let (clipped, truncated) = truncate_for_audit(&e.to_string());
            ExitStatus::Err {
                message: clipped,
                truncated,
            }
        }
    };

    ToolDispatch {
        result: raw_result,
        audit: AuditMeta {
            step_id,
            started_at,
            finished_at,
            args_hash,
            side_effect,
            exit_status,
        },
    }
}
```

(`touched` recording stays on the registry ÔÇö it's a per-turn collector,
not permission policy. The pipeline doesn't need it.)

### 3. `src/tools/permission_pipeline.rs` ÔÇö tests for each stage

Add `#[cfg(test)] mod tests` to the new file. Each test constructs a
`PermissionPipeline` directly (no `ToolRegistry` needed) and exercises
one stage. Required tests:

- `check_allows_when_no_permissions_configured` ÔÇö pipeline built with
  `permissive()`, unknown tool name, expect `Ok(())` and no
  side-effects.
- `check_denies_in_strict_mode_for_unknown_tool` ÔÇö pipeline with
  `permission_mode = Strict`, permissions installed but no allow rule
  for the tool, expect `Err(Error::PermissionDenied { reason: Mode(Strict) })`.
- `check_runs_auto_classifier_in_auto_mode` ÔÇö pipeline with
  `permission_mode = Auto` and a stub classifier that returns
  `Ok((true, "blocked"))`, expect `Err(Error::PermissionDenied { reason: Mode(Auto) })`.
  The stub classifier should record that it was called.
- `check_returns_over_limit_error_when_tracker_saturated` ÔÇö same
  setup, classifier's `tracker.is_over_limit()` returns `true`,
  expect `Err(Error::PermissionDeniedLimit { .. })`.
- `check_invokes_permission_hook_for_interactive_tool_in_non_headless_mode` ÔÇö
  hook returns `Deny("nope")`, expect
  `Err(Error::PermissionDenied { reason: Hook { name: "nope" } })`.
- `check_hook_transform_replaces_arguments` ÔÇö hook returns
  `Transform(json!({"command": "ls"}))`, expect `Ok(())` and
  `arguments["command"] == "ls"` in the caller's value.
- `check_runs_external_hook_in_headless_mode` ÔÇö headless=true, no
  external hooks registered, interactive tool, expect
  `Err(Error::PermissionDenied { reason: Hook { name: "PermissionRequest" } })`.
- `check_l1_policy_denies_disallowed_shell` ÔÇö policy has
  `disallowed_pattern = ["rm -rf /"]`, call with `command = "rm -rf /"`,
  expect `Err(Error::PolicyViolation { .. })` (or whatever the existing
  error variant is ÔÇö read `policy_sandbox::PolicyConfig::check_shell`'s
  return type to confirm).
- `check_l1_policy_denies_disallowed_fs_path` ÔÇö policy with a
  protected path, call with `path = "/etc/passwd"` on `Write`, expect
  an error.

For the `Auto` mode and `Auto` denial-limit tests, the existing
`AutoClassifier::classify` signature may require a real or stub LLM
provider. Read `src/tools/auto_classifier.rs` to see how to construct
a minimal one. If a stub LLM is required, use `MockProvider` from the
test harness.

### 4. `src/tools/mod.rs` ÔÇö update existing tests

The existing `invoke_with_audit` tests in `src/tools/mod.rs::tests`
(grep for `invoke_with_audit` in the `mod tests` block) likely build
a `ToolRegistry` and call `invoke_with_audit` directly. These should
continue to pass with **no changes** ÔÇö the public signature and
behavior of `invoke_with_audit` are preserved. If a test fails
because it poked at a removed field directly, fix the test to use the
new builder method or to construct a `PermissionPipeline` and call
`pipeline.check` directly. **No production behavior changes are
allowed.**

### 5. Verify

```bash
cargo test --lib tools::
cargo test --lib runtime::
cargo test --bin recursive
cargo clippy --all-targets --all-features -- -D warnings
cargo fmt --all
```

All must be clean. The new file is `src/tools/permission_pipeline.rs`
plus possibly a small adjustment in `src/tools/mod.rs`. Existing
permission-related tests should all pass unchanged.

## Acceptance

- A new struct `PermissionPipeline` exists in
  `src/tools/permission_pipeline.rs` (or equivalent location).
- `ToolRegistry::invoke_with_audit` is at most 60 lines (down from
  281), with permission logic delegated to `permission_pipeline.check`.
- `tools/mod.rs` shrinks by ~200 lines.
- At least 8 new tests cover each stage of `PermissionPipeline::check`
  in isolation.
- All existing tests in `src/tools/mod.rs::tests`, `src/runtime.rs`,
  and the binary continue to pass with no source-level changes.
- `cargo test`, `cargo clippy -D warnings`, `cargo fmt` all clean.

## Notes for the agent

- **Read first**: `src/tools/mod.rs:735-1016` (the function you're
  extracting) and `src/tools/mod.rs:287-321` (the struct whose fields
  you're moving). Also read `src/permissions/mod.rs:309` and `:424`
  for the `check_static` and `any_interactive` methods you'll be
  calling.
- **The Transform branch** (line 837) is the trickiest part. The
  hook's `Transform(new_args)` mutates `arguments` in place. Your
  pipeline must do the same: take `arguments: &mut Value`, modify
  it, and continue. The caller's `arguments` will reflect the
  transform because the caller passes a `&mut Value` from its own
  owned `Value`.
- **Lock discipline**: the current code drops the read guard at lines
  826, 873, 903, 929 to avoid holding the lock across an `await`.
  Preserve this exactly. Holding a `tokio::sync::RwLock` read guard
  across `await` is a soundness bug (it can block writers forever).
- **L1 policy check**: it's lines 945-972. This belongs in the
  pipeline (it's a policy check) but the **touched-files recording**
  at lines 933-936 does NOT belong in the pipeline (it's
  observability, not permission). Make sure the pipeline's `check`
  does the policy check but the `invoke_with_audit` still does the
  `record_touched` call.
- **`AutoClassifier::classify` takes `&mut self`** (see comment at
  `src/tools/mod.rs:319`). The pipeline holds it inside an
  `Arc<tokio::sync::Mutex<...>>` and locks it at call time, just like
  the current code.
- **No public API changes.** The `ToolRegistry` builder must keep
  working. If a caller currently does
  `ToolRegistryBuilder::new().with_permissions(...).build()`, that
  call site must continue to compile.
- **Imports**: the new file will need `crate::agent::types::PermissionDecision`,
  `crate::error::Error`, `crate::hooks::ExternalHookRunner`,
  `crate::permissions::*`, `crate::policy_sandbox`, and
  `crate::tools::auto_classifier::AutoClassifier`. Re-use whatever's
  already imported in `src/tools/mod.rs`.

## Out of scope (DO NOT do these)

- Don't change the public signature of `ToolRegistry::invoke_with_audit`.
- Don't change any other method on `ToolRegistry` (registration,
  `find_by_name`, `is_readonly`, etc.).
- Don't change `Permission`, `PermissionMode`, `PermissionDecision`,
  or any enum variant in `permissions/mod.rs` or `agent/types.rs`.
- Don't refactor the L1 policy check itself ÔÇö just move it.
- Don't add a new error variant. The pipeline must reuse the existing
  `Error::PermissionDenied`, `Error::PermissionDeniedLimit`,
  `Error::PolicyViolation`, etc.
- Don't extract `TouchedFiles` recording. It stays on the registry
  as a per-turn collector, called from `invoke_with_audit` between
  the pipeline check and the tool dispatch.
- Don't change any `src/tools/*` file other than `mod.rs` and the
  new `permission_pipeline.rs`. The other tools are unaware of the
  refactor.
- Don't touch `agent.rs::Agent::run`. This is `tools::` work.
```

# rust-patch-discipline

## When to apply this skill

Trigger words: `apply_patch`, `V4A`, "patch rejected", "ambiguous
context", "Update File", any time the previous `apply_patch` call
returned an error.

## V4A in 60 seconds

```text
*** Begin Patch
*** Update File: <relative-path>
@@ <first-anchor-line>
 <unchanged context line>
-<line to remove>
+<line to add>
 <another unchanged context line>
*** End Patch
```

**Critical rules**:

1. **Anchor (`@@ ...`) must be unique within the file.** If three
   lines look identical (e.g. test `let mut x = ...`), the patcher
   will reject with "ambiguous context".

2. **Context lines (` `-prefixed) must match the file byte-for-byte.**
   Even leading whitespace matters. Re-read the section with
   `read_file` if you're not certain.

3. **One hunk

//! Static tool permission configuration.
//!
//! Provides a layered permission system where rules from different sources
//! (user config, project config, session) are merged with well-defined
//! semantics:
//!
//! - **deny**: any layer denies ÔåÆ denied (union)
//! - **allow**: any layer allows ÔåÆ allowed (union)
//! - **interactive**: any layer marks as interactive ÔåÆ interactive (union)
//!
//! The session-level [`PermissionMode`] provides additional runtime behaviour

//!
//! Structured error types that library consumers can match on.

use crate::permissions::DecisionReason;
use thiserror::Error;

pub type Result<T, E = Error> = std::result::Result<T, E>;

#[derive(Debug, Error)]
pub enum Error {

## Plan for Goal 261

**Goal:** Extract a `PermissionPipeline` type from `ToolRegistry::invoke_with_audit` so the orchestration of permission checks, policy validation, and policy re-check on Transform is testable in isolation. The current `invoke_with_audit` function in `src/tools/mod.rs` (lines ~675-895) is ~220 lines and contains five distinct phases:

1. **Static permission check** (lines 730-770): read shared permissions lock, call `check_static`, handle Denied/Unknown/Allowed results
2. **Auto mode classifier** (lines 740-770): for Auto mode, classify via LLM before static check
3. **Strict mode handling** (lines 800-815): if `perm_is_unknown` and Strict ÔåÆ deny
4. **Hook delegation** (lines 820-860): for non-headless + interactive + Unknown, call `PermissionHook` and re-check policy on Transform
5. **Headless external hook** (lines 880-905): for headless + interactive, call `ExternalHookRunner`
6. **L1 policy check** (lines 950-985): shell/fs policy enforcement before tool execution
7. **Unknown warning** (lines 906-916): trace warning for implicitly allowed tools

Wait, looking more carefully, the phases actually are:
- Phase A: `safety_content_for_tool` (line 731) ÔÇö extract file path
- Phase B: Auto mode classifier (lines 740-770) 
- Phase C: `check_static` permission check (lines 780-800) ÔÇö Denied/Unknown/Allowed
- Phase D: Strict mode handling (lines 800-815)
- Phase E: Hook delegation for non-headless interactive (lines 820-870)
- Phase F: Headless external hook (lines 880-905)
- Phase G: Implicit allow warning (lines 906-916)
- Phase H: touched_files recording (lines 925-928)
- Phase I: Tool not found check (lines 930-940)
- Phase J: L1 policy check (lines 947-985)
- Phase K: Side effect, step_id, hash, span, execute (lines 987-1030)
- Phase L: AuditMeta construction (lines 1030-1050)

The goal is to extract **only the permission-check phases** (A through J) ÔÇö i.e., everything that happens before the tool is actually executed.

The key design choices:
1. **`PermissionPipeline` should be a new struct** in `src/tools/permission_pipeline.rs` that holds the configuration needed to run the check (or borrows from the registry)
2. It should expose **one or more public methods** that do the pre-tool permission work
3. The extracted logic should be **behavior-preserving** ÔÇö every existing test should still pass
4. **Public API addition only** ÔÇö no changes to existing struct fields or method signatures
5. We need at least one new test for the pipeline (preferably more)
6. We need to handle the `mut arguments` issue (the hook may Transform arguments)

Let me think about the right shape. Given the complexity, the natural API would be:

```rust
pub struct PermissionPipeline<'a> {
    permissions: Option<&'a SharedPermissions>,
    auto_classifier: Option<&'a Arc<tokio::sync::Mutex<AutoClassifier>>>,
    permission_mode: &'a PermissionMode,
    permission_hook: Option<&'a Arc<dyn PermissionHook>>,
    headless: bool,
    hook_runner: &'a ExternalHookRunner,
    policy: Option<&'a PolicyConfig>,
}

pub struct PipelineDecision {
    /// Final arguments (possibly transformed by a hook)
    pub arguments: Value,
    /// If the pipeline denied the call, this carries the error
    pub deny: Option<(Error, AuditMeta)>,
}

impl<'a> PermissionPipeline<'a> {
    pub fn from_registry(registry: &'a ToolRegistry) -> Self { ... }
    
    /// Run all pre-execution permission checks.
    /// Returns either a denial (with audit) or the (possibly transformed) arguments.
    pub async fn check(&self, tool_name: &str, arguments: Value) -> PipelineDecision { ... }
    
    /// Re-check L1 policy on transformed arguments. Hooks that return
    /// `Transform` could substitute args that bypass the original policy check.
    pub fn recheck_policy(&self, tool_name: &str, arguments: &Value) -> Result<()> { ... }
}
```

Actually, looking at the existing code, the natural split is:
- **`PermissionPipeline::check`**: runs the static permission check, auto mode, strict handling, hook delegation, and headless external hook ÔÇö returns a `PipelineDecision` with either denial or final args
- **`PermissionPipeline::recheck_policy`**: re-runs the L1 policy check (used in two places: original call site, and after hook Transform)

Wait, but the L1 policy check (section J) runs after all permission checks pass. If we want to "extract the pre-execution permission checks" cleanly, we should put L1 policy in the pipeline too.

Let me re-read the goal:
> Move the 7 pre-execution permission-check phases (lines 730-915) out of `invoke_with_audit` into a new `PermissionPipeline::check` method. Keep lines 920+ (touched_files, tool lookup, side effect, execute, audit) in `invoke_with_audit`. The pipeline must also expose a `recheck_policy` method (used today at lines 856-877 when a hook returns `Transform`) so callers can re-run L1 policy on hook-mutated args.

So the pipeline owns:
- safety_content extraction
- auto classifier
- check_static
- strict mode
- hook delegation
- headless external hook
- implicit allow warning
- L1 policy check (the FIRST one, not just the recheck)
- recheck_policy (the second one, post-hook-Transform)

What stays in `invoke_with_audit`:
- touched_files recording
- tool lookup
- side_effect, step_id, args_hash, started_at
- tool.execute call
- audit construction
- ToolDispatch return

The `recheck_policy` is its own method because it's called both in the original code path (lines 947-985) AND inside the hook Transform branch (lines 856-877).

Hmm, wait ÔÇö looking at the code more carefully:

Lines 856-877: This is the **re-check on Transform** ÔÇö re-run shell/fs policy on the new args. This is inside the hook delegation block.

Lines 947-985: This is the **original L1 policy check** that runs for ALL tool calls (whether or not they went through hook Transform).

The goal says:
> The pipeline must also expose a `recheck_policy` method (used today at lines 856-877 when a hook returns `Transform`) so callers can re-run L1 policy on hook-mutated args.

So `recheck_policy` is a separate method that can be called by hook-mutated code paths. The main check method probably uses it internally too (or the original L1 check is also in the pipeline).

Looking at the goal more carefully, I think the cleanest design is:

```rust
impl PermissionPipeline {
    /// Run the full pre-execution permission check. Returns either a
    /// `PermissionDecision::Deny` with audit metadata, or `Allow(arguments)`
    /// where `arguments` is the (possibly hook-transformed) final args.
    pub async fn check(&self, name: &str, arguments: Value) -> CheckOutcome { ... }
    
    /// Re-run the L1 policy check on potentially hook-mutated arguments.
    /// Used by `check()` internally after a hook returns `Transform`, and
    /// exposed publicly so external callers can re-check policy.
    pub fn recheck_policy(&self, name: &str, arguments: &Value) -> Result<(), Error> { ... }
}
```

The `CheckOutcome` would be something like:
```rust
pub enum CheckOutcome {
    Deny { error: Error, audit: AuditMeta },
    Allow { arguments: Value },
}
```

This way, `invoke_with_audit` becomes:

```rust
pub async fn invoke_with_audit(&self, name: &str, mut arguments: Value) -> ToolDispatch {
    // Delegate to permission pipeline.
    let pipeline = PermissionPipeline::new(self);
    match pipeline.check(name, arguments).await {
        CheckOutcome::Deny { error, audit } => {
            return ToolDispatch { result: Err(error), audit };
        }
        CheckOutcome::Allow { arguments: final_args } => {
            arguments = final_args;
        }
    }
    
    // Record touched files for the active turn.
    if let Some(slot) = &self.touched {
        record_touched(name, &arguments, slot);
    }

    let Some(tool) = self.find_by_name(name) else {
        return ToolDispatch {
            result: Err(Error::UnknownTool(name.into())),
            audit: AuditMeta::synthetic_unknown_tool(name),
        };
    };

    // ... rest of execution logic (side_effect, step_id, execute, audit) ...
}
```

This is much cleaner. Let me verify by counting: lines 730-915 is ~185 lines extracted. The remaining `invoke_with_audit` would be much smaller.

But wait ÔÇö what about the hook delegation block? It also re-runs the L1 policy check on Transform. Looking at the goal:
> The pipeline must also expose a `recheck_policy` method (used today at lines 856-877 when a hook returns `Transform`) so callers can re-run L1 policy on hook-mutated args.

So `recheck_policy` is the SECOND call (lines 856-877). The FIRST call (lines 947-985) is just the L1 policy check that runs in the main path.

Hmm, actually they are functionally equivalent ÔÇö both check the L1 policy on the given arguments. So one method `recheck_policy(name, args)` works for both. The first call is in the main path (after all permission checks), and the second is inside the hook delegation.

Actually wait, looking again at the code:

```
// Goal-212: When no rule explicitly matched (Unknown) and the tool
// is in the interactive list, delegate to the registered
// PermissionHook as a safety net ...
if perm_is_unknown && !self.headless && is_interactive_tool {
    if let Some(hook) = &self.permission_hook {
        drop(guard);
        match hook.check(name, &arguments).await {
            PermissionDecision::Deny(reason) => { ... }
            PermissionDecision::Transform(new_args) => {
                // Re-run policy check on the transformed arguments.
                // A malicious/compromised hook could use `updated_input`
                // to substitute a different command/path that bypasses
                // the policy check already performed above.
                if let Some(ref policy) = self.policy {
                    if let Some(cmd) = new_args.get("command").and_then(|v| v.as_str())
                    {
                        if let Err(e) = policy.check_shell(cmd) {
                            return ToolDispatch {
                                result: Err(e),
                                audit: AuditMeta::synthetic_unknown_tool(name),
                            };
                        }
                    }
                    let is_write = matches!(name, "Write" | "Edit" | "StrReplace");
                    let path_arg = new_args
                        .get("path")
                        .or_else(|| new_args.get("file_path"))
                        .and_then(|v| v.as_str());
                    if let Some(path) = path_arg {
                        if let Err(e) = policy.check_fs_path(path, is_write) {
                            return ToolDispatch {
                                result: Err(e),
                                audit: AuditMeta::synthetic_unknown_tool(name),
                            };
                        }
                    }
                }
                arguments = new_args;
            }
            PermissionDecision::Allow => {}
        }
    } else {
        drop(guard);
    }
} else
```

So the recheck_policy method needs to be:
- Look at `new_args` (the hook's transform)
- Check shell command if `command` field present  
- Check file path if `path` or `file_path` field present
- Return the error if policy fails

The FIRST L1 policy check (in the main path, lines 947-985) does the same thing but on the original arguments. So the `recheck_policy` method can serve both purposes.

> Add at least 1 new test (preferably more) covering: at least the `recheck_policy` method

So I need to write at least one test for `recheck_policy`. I should also write tests for the main `check` method.

Let me think about what tests to write:

1. **`recheck_policy` accepts clean args** ÔÇö args without `command` or `path` fields ÔåÆ Ok
2. **`recheck_policy` denies shell policy violation** ÔÇö args with bad `command` ÔåÆ policy error
3. **`recheck_policy` denies fs policy violation** ÔÇö args with bad `path` ÔåÆ policy error
4. **`recheck_policy` passes after Transform with good args** ÔÇö hook transforms, then recheck passes
5. **`PermissionPipeline::check` denies denied tool** ÔÇö straightforward denial
6. **`PermissionPipeline::check` allows read-only tool with no rules** ÔÇö Unknown ÔåÆ Allow (non-interactive, non-strict)
7. **`PermissionPipeline::check` handles Transform with recheck** ÔÇö hook transforms, recheck OK
8. **`PermissionPipeline::check` handles Transform with policy failure** ÔÇö hook transforms to bad args ÔåÆ deny

Wait, since the PermissionPipeline is a public API addition, I can add a comprehensive set of tests for it. But the goal says "at least 1 new test (preferably more) covering: at least the `recheck_policy` method" ÔÇö so I should prioritize the recheck_policy tests and add a few more if it makes sense.

Let me think about the field structure of PermissionPipeline. The goal says:
> Move the 7 pre-execution permission-check phases (lines 730-915) out of `invoke_with_audit` into a new `PermissionPipeline::check` method.

So the pipeline needs access to:
- `permissions` (Option<SharedPermissions>) ÔÇö for read().await
- `auto_classifier` (Option<Arc<Mutex<AutoClassifier>>>) ÔÇö for Auto mode
- `permission_mode` (PermissionMode) ÔÇö already snapshotted in ToolRegistry
- `permission_hook` (Option<Arc<dyn PermissionHook>>) ÔÇö for hook delegation
- `headless` (bool) ÔÇö for headless mode dispatch
- `hook_runner` (ExternalHookRunner) ÔÇö for headless external hooks
- `policy` (Option<PolicyConfig>) ÔÇö for L1 policy check

The pipeline should borrow from the registry. Two options:
1. Hold `&ToolRegistry` and access fields directly ÔÇö simpler but tight coupling
2. Hold individual `&` references to the fields ÔÇö more decoupled, but more complex

Actually, the cleanest design is to have the pipeline hold a reference to the registry. The "decoupling" benefit of extraction is more about testability and clarity than decoupling from ToolRegistry. Plus, in `invoke_with_audit`, we have `&self` access to ToolRegistry fields anyway.

Let me go with: `PermissionPipeline<'a> { registry: &'a ToolRegistry }`. The pipeline methods can then access `self.registry.permissions`, etc.

Actually, wait ÔÇö `permission_hook` is `Option<Arc<dyn PermissionHook>>` which has a `check` method that takes `&self`. And `Arc<dyn PermissionHook>` is fine to clone (it's an Arc). And the `auto_classifier` is `Option<Arc<tokio::sync::Mutex<AutoClassifier>>>`. All of these are Clone, and the references don't need to be exclusive.

OK, let me design:

```rust
// src/tools/permission_pipeline.rs

//! Pre-execution permission pipeline for tool dispatch.
//!
//! Extracted from `ToolRegistry::invoke_with_audit` (Goal 261). Owns the
//! seven pre-execution phases:
//!
//! 1. Safety content extraction (file-path content for protected-path check)
//! 2. Auto-mode LLM classifier (Goal 200)
//! 3. Static permission check (`check_static`)
//! 4. Strict-mode handling (deny Unknown tools in Strict mode)
//! 5. Hook delegation (non-headless + interactive + Unknown ÔåÆ `PermissionHook`)
//! 6. Headless external hook dispatch
//! 7. L1 policy check (shell/fs policies from `PolicyConfig`)
//!
//! The pipeline is reference-bound to a `ToolRegistry` and borrows its
//! configuration. Constructing a pipeline is cheap; the expensive part is
//! the permission check itself, which may await on shared locks, the
//! auto-classifier, and the headless hook runner.

use async_trait::async_trait;
use serde_json::Value;

use crate::agent::PermissionDecision;
use crate::error::{Error, Result};
use crate::permissions::auto_classifier::AutoClassifier;
use crate::permissions::{DecisionReason, Permission, PermissionMode, SharedPermissions};
use crate::policy_sandbox::PolicyConfig;

use super::{AuditMeta, PermissionHook, ToolRegistry};

/// Outcome of a permission-pipeline check.
#[derive(Debug)]
pub enum CheckOutcome {
    /// Pipeline denied the call. Carries the structured error and a
    /// synthetic audit record.
    Deny { error: Error, audit: AuditMeta },
    /// Pipeline allowed the call. `arguments` is the (possibly hook-
    /// transformed) final arguments to pass to the tool.
    Allow { arguments: Value },
}

impl CheckOutcome {
    /// True if the pipeline denied the call.
    pub fn is_deny(&self) -> bool {
        matches!(self, CheckOutcome::Deny { .. })
    }
}

/// Pre-execution permission pipeline.
pub struct PermissionPipeline<'a> {
    registry: &'a ToolRegistry,
}

impl<'a> PermissionPipeline<'a> {
    /// Construct a pipeline that borrows configuration from `registry`.
    pub fn new(registry: &'a ToolRegistry) -> Self {
        Self { registry }
    }

    /// Run all pre-execution permission checks for `tool_name` with
    /// `arguments`. Returns either a denial (with audit metadata) or the
    /// final arguments to pass to the tool.
    ///
    /// This is a behavior-preserving extraction from
    /// `ToolRegistry::invoke_with_audit`. The semantics of every code
    /// path are unchanged.
    pub async fn check(&self, tool_name: &str, mut arguments: Value) -> CheckOutcome {
        // ... (extract logic from lines 730-915) ...
    }

    /// Re-run the L1 policy check on `arguments`. Used internally after
    /// a hook returns `Transform` (to catch a hook that mutates args to
    /// bypass the original policy check), and exposed publicly so callers
    /// can validate hook-mutated arguments before re-dispatch.
    pub fn recheck_policy(&self, tool_name: &str, arguments: &Value) -> Result<()> {
        // ... (extract logic from lines 856-877) ...
    }
}
```

Wait, I need to think about the location of `PermissionHook` import. In the current `mod.rs`, `PermissionHook` is defined as `pub trait PermissionHook: Send + Sync`. It's in the same module as `ToolRegistry`. So when I import it from `permission_pipeline.rs`, I need to use `super::PermissionHook` or import it via the parent module.

Also, I need to think about whether the `PermissionPipeline` should expose more internals or not. Looking at the goal:
> exposes a `recheck_policy` method (used today at lines 856-877 when a hook returns `Transform`) so callers can re-run L1 policy on hook-mutated args

The "callers" here presumably means external callers, like the test suite. So `recheck_policy` is a public method. The `check` method is also clearly public.

OK let me think about edge cases in the recheck_policy. The original code (lines 856-877) is:
```rust
if let Some(ref policy) = self.policy {
    if let Some(cmd) = new_args.get("command").and_then(|v| v.as_str())
    {
        if let Err(e) = policy.check_shell(cmd) {
            return ToolDispatch {
                result: Err(e),
                audit: AuditMeta::synthetic_unknown_tool(name),
            };
        }
    }
    let is_write = matches!(name, "Write" | "Edit" | "StrReplace");
    let path_arg = new_args
        .get("path")
        .or_else(|| new_args.get("file_path"))
        .and_then(|v| v.as_str());
    if let Some(path) = path_arg {
        if let Err(e) = policy.check_fs_path(path, is_write) {
            return ToolDispatch {
                result: Err(e),
                audit: AuditMeta::synthetic_unknown_tool(name),
            };
        }
    }
}
```

This is a pure policy check on arguments. It returns nothing on success, and `Result<(), Error>` (or specifically, the policy error) on failure. The `policy` field is `Option<&PolicyConfig>`. If `policy` is None, the function does nothing and returns Ok.

Wait, but `policy_sandbox::PolicyConfig` is imported. Let me check the import path:

Looking at the imports in mod.rs:
```rust
use crate::permissions::auto_classifier::AutoClassifier;
use crate::permissions::SharedPermissions;
use crate::permissions::{DecisionReason, Permission, PermissionMode, PermissionsConfig};
```

And `policy_sandbox::PolicyConfig` is referenced as `policy_sandbox::PolicyConfig` in the struct field. In `mod.rs` line 308, the field is `policy: Option<policy_sandbox::PolicyConfig>` ÔÇö uses inline path because there's no `use` statement.

For the new `permission_pipeline.rs` file, I'll add the necessary `use` statements.

Let me also look at the `Permission` and `DecisionReason` types to make sure I import them correctly. They're already used in `mod.rs`, so I know the import path is `crate::permissions::{DecisionReason, Permission, PermissionMode}`.

Now, the policy_sandbox module is at `src/tools/policy_sandbox.rs`. Let me check its exports:
- `pub use` of `FsPolicy`, `PolicyConfig`, `ShellPolicy` in mod.rs lines 232-234.

So in `permission_pipeline.rs` I can write `use crate::tools::policy_sandbox::PolicyConfig;` or `use super::policy_sandbox::PolicyConfig;` (since `permission_pipeline.rs` is a sibling module of `policy_sandbox` in `tools`).

Let me also think about the `recheck_policy` method. Its return type should be `Result<(), Error>` since policy.check_shell/check_fs_path return `Result<_, Error>`. If no policy is configured, it returns `Ok(())`. If policy check fails, it returns `Err(e)` with the policy error.

Now let me start writing the code.

Actually, one more design consideration: should the `PermissionPipeline` hold the `ToolRegistry` by reference, or should it own all the necessary fields? 

Pros of holding `&ToolRegistry`:
- Simple construction
- Always up-to-date with registry config
- Less duplication

Cons:
- Slight coupling to `ToolRegistry` internals
- Can't construct a `PermissionPipeline` without a `ToolRegistry` (limits standalone testability)

For now, I'll go with holding `&ToolRegistry`. The pipeline can later be made more standalone if needed.

    /// Returns `Ok(())` when `command` is permitted, `Err(PermissionDenied)`
    /// when it matches a deny pattern.
    pub fn check_shell(&self, command: &str) -> Result<()> {
        for pattern in &self.shell.deny_patterns {
            if command.contains(pattern.as_str()) {
                return Err(Error::PermissionDenied {
                    name: format!("shell command blocked by policy: matches pattern `{pattern}`"),
                    reason: DecisionReason::Rule {
                        source: RuleSource::Project,
                        pattern: pattern.clone(),
                    },
                });
            }
        }
        Ok(())
    }

Good, `check_shell` and `check_fs_path` return `Result<(), Error>`. So `recheck_policy` returns `Result<(), Error>` and the caller can decide what to do with the error.

Now let me design the PermissionPipeline API more concretely. I want:

1. `PermissionPipeline<'a>` struct with `&'a ToolRegistry`
2. `CheckOutcome` enum with `Deny { error, audit }` and `Allow { arguments }` variants
3. `check(name, args) -> CheckOutcome` ÔÇö runs all 7 phases
4. `recheck_policy(name, args) -> Result<(), Error>` ÔÇö runs the L1 policy check

Now I need to write tests. Let me think about what tests to add:

For `recheck_policy`:
1. `recheck_policy_with_no_policy_returns_ok` ÔÇö registry with no policy ÔåÆ recheck_policy returns Ok regardless of args
2. `recheck_policy_with_clean_shell_returns_ok` ÔÇö policy configured, but command doesn't match ÔåÆ Ok
3. `recheck_policy_blocks_blocked_shell_command` ÔÇö policy with denied shell pattern, command matches ÔåÆ Err
4. `recheck_policy_with_clean_path_returns_ok` ÔÇö policy configured, path doesn't match deny ÔåÆ Ok
5. `recheck_policy_blocks_blocked_path` ÔÇö policy with denied path prefix, path matches ÔåÆ Err
6. `recheck_policy_with_write_tool` ÔÇö path matches, write=true, is_write tool name ÔåÆ check
7. `recheck_policy_uses_file_path_field_for_edit_tool` ÔÇö Edit uses file_path field

For `check`:
1. `check_denies_explicitly_denied_tool` ÔÇö tool in deny list ÔåÆ Deny
2. `check_allows_explicitly_allowed_tool` ÔÇö tool in allow list ÔåÆ Allow
3. `check_strict_mode_denies_unknown_tool` ÔÇö Strict mode + Unknown tool ÔåÆ Deny
4. `check_default_mode_allows_unknown_tool` ÔÇö Default mode + Unknown tool ÔåÆ Allow
5. `check_deny_hook_blocks_call` ÔÇö hook returns Deny ÔåÆ Deny
6. `check_transform_hook_rewrites_args` ÔÇö hook returns Transform ÔåÆ Allow with new args
7. `check_transform_with_policy_violation_denies` ÔÇö hook transforms to bad args ÔåÆ Deny
8. `check_records_audit_on_deny` ÔÇö verify AuditMeta is populated
9. `check_auto_mode_classifier_blocks` ÔÇö Auto mode + classifier denies ÔåÆ Deny

```rust
// src/tools/permission_pipeline.rs

//! Pre-execution permission pipeline for tool dispatch.
//!
//! ...

use serde_json::Value;

use crate::agent::PermissionDecision;
use crate::error::{Error, Result};
use crate::permissions::{DecisionReason, PermissionMode, SharedPermissions};
use super::policy_sandbox::PolicyConfig;
use super::{AuditMeta, ToolRegistry};

/// Outcome of a permission-pipeline check.
pub enum CheckOutcome {
    Deny { error: Error, audit: AuditMeta },
    Allow { arguments: Value },
}

pub struct PermissionPipeline<'a> {
    registry: &'a ToolRegistry,
}

impl<'a> PermissionPipeline<'a> {
    pub fn new(registry: &'a ToolRegistry) -> Self {
        Self { registry }
    }

    pub async fn check(&self, tool_name: &str, mut arguments: Value) -> CheckOutcome {
        // Phase 1: Safety content extraction
        let safety_content = safety_content_for_tool(tool_name, &arguments);
        
        // Phase 2-3: Permission check (Auto mode + Static check)
        if let Some(ref sp) = self.registry.permissions {
            let guard = sp.read().await;
            
            // Auto mode classifier
            if matches!(guard.mode, PermissionMode::Auto) {
                if let Some(ref classifier) = self.registry.auto_classifier {
                    let args_summary = serde_json::to_string(&arguments).unwrap_or_else(|_| "{}".into());
                    let mut c = classifier.lock().await;
                    match c.classify(tool_name, &args_summary, "").await {
                        Ok((true, _reason)) => {
                            if c.tracker.is_over_limit() {
                                return CheckOutcome::Deny {
                                    error: Error::PermissionDeniedLimit { name: tool_name.into() },
                                    audit: AuditMeta::synthetic_unknown_tool(tool_name),
                                };
                            }
                            return CheckOutcome::Deny {
                                error: Error::PermissionDenied {
                                    name: tool_name.into(),
                                    reason: DecisionReason::Mode(PermissionMode::Auto),
                                },
                                audit: AuditMeta::synthetic_unknown_tool(tool_name),
                            };
                        }
                        Ok((false, _)) => { /* fall through to static check */ }
                        Err(_e) => { /* classifier error ÔåÆ conservative: allow */ }
                    }
                }
            }
            
            // Static check
            let is_readonly = self.registry.is_readonly(tool_name);
            let is_interactive_tool = guard.any_interactive(tool_name);
            let mut perm_is_unknown = false;
            match guard.check_static(tool_name, is_readonly, safety_content.as_deref()) {
                Permission::Denied(reason, _msg) => {
                    return CheckOutcome::Deny {
                        error: Error::PermissionDenied {
                            name: tool_name.into(),
                            reason: reason.clone(),
                        },
                        audit: AuditMeta::synthetic_unknown_tool(tool_name),
                    };
                }
                Permission::Unknown => {
                    perm_is_unknown = true;
                }
                Permission::Allowed(_) => {}
            }
            
            // Phase 4: Strict mode
            if perm_is_unknown && matches!(guard.mode, PermissionMode::Strict) {
                return CheckOutcome::Deny {
                    error: Error::PermissionDenied {
                        name: tool_name.into(),
                        reason: DecisionReason::Mode(PermissionMode::Strict),
                    },
                    audit: AuditMeta::synthetic_unknown_tool(tool_name),
                };
            }
            
            // Phase 5: Hook delegation (non-headless + interactive + Unknown)
            if perm_is_unknown && !self.registry.headless && is_interactive_tool {
                if let Some(hook) = &self.registry.permission_hook {
                    drop(guard);
                    match hook.check(tool_name, &arguments).await {
                        PermissionDecision::Deny(reason) => {
                            return CheckOutcome::Deny {
                                error: Error::PermissionDenied {
                                    name: tool_name.into(),
                                    reason: DecisionReason::Hook { name: reason },
                                },
                                audit: AuditMeta::synthetic_unknown_tool(tool_name),
                            };
                        }
                        PermissionDecision::Transform(new_args) => {
                            if let Err(e) = self.recheck_policy(tool_name, &new_args) {
                                return CheckOutcome::Deny {
                                    error: e,
                                    audit: AuditMeta::synthetic_unknown_tool(tool_name),
                                };
                            }
                            arguments = new_args;
                        }
                        PermissionDecision::Allow => {}
                    }
                } else {
                    drop(guard);
                }
            }
            // Phase 6: Headless external hook
            else if self.registry.headless && is_interactive_tool {
                if self.registry.hook_runner.is_empty() {
                    return CheckOutcome::Deny {
                        error: Error::PermissionDenied {
                            name: tool_name.into(),
                            reason: DecisionReason::Hook {
                                name: "PermissionRequest".into(),
                            },
                        },
                        audit: AuditMeta::synthetic_unknown_tool(tool_name),
                    };
                }
                let hook_input = crate::hooks::external::HookInput {
                    event: crate::hooks::external::HookEvent::PermissionRequest,
                    tool_name: Some(tool_name.to_string()),
                    args: Some(arguments.clone()),
                    mode: format!("{:?}", self.registry.permission_mode),
                    content: None,
                    message: None,
                    depth: None,
                    reason: None,
                    error: None,
                };
                drop(guard);
                let hook_result = self.registry.hook_runner.dispatch(&hook_input).await;
                if !matches!(hook_result.action, crate::hooks::HookAction::Continue) {
                    return CheckOutcome::Deny {
                        error: Error::PermissionDenied {
                            name: tool_name.into(),
                            reason: DecisionReason::Hook {
                                name: "PermissionRequest".into(),
                            },
                        },
                        audit: AuditMeta::synthetic_unknown_tool(tool_name),
                    };
                }
            }
            // Phase 7: Implicit allow warning
            else {
                if perm_is_unknown {
                    tracing::warn!(
                        tool = %tool_name,
                        "tool has no explicit permission rule; \
                         allowing implicitly (use strict mode to deny by default)"
                    );
                }
                drop(guard);
            }
        }
        
        // Phase 8: L1 policy check
        if let Err(e) = self.recheck_policy(tool_name, &arguments) {
            return CheckOutcome::Deny {
                error: e,
                audit: AuditMeta::synthetic_unknown_tool(tool_name),
            };
        }
        
        CheckOutcome::Allow { arguments }
    }

    pub fn recheck_policy(&self, tool_name: &str, arguments: &Value) -> Result<()> {
        let Some(policy) = self.registry.policy.as_ref() else {
            return Ok(());
        };
        if let Some(cmd) = arguments.get("command").and_then(|v| v.as_str()) {
            policy.check_shell(cmd)?;
        }
        let is_write = matches!(tool_name, "Write" | "Edit" | "StrReplace");
        let path_arg = arguments
            .get("path")
            .or_else(|| arguments.get("file_path"))
            .and_then(|v| v.as_str());
        if let Some(path) = path_arg {
            policy.check_fs_path(path, is_write)?;
        }
        Ok(())
    }
}

/// Extract the file-path "content" from tool arguments for the safety
/// check in `check_static`. (Same logic as the existing
/// `safety_content_for_tool` in `mod.rs`.)
fn safety_content_for_tool(name: &str, args: &serde_json::Value) -> Option<String> {
    match name {
        "Write" | "Read" => args["path"].as_str().map(String::from),
        "Edit" => args["file_path"].as_str().map(String::from),
        _ => None,
    }
}
```

Wait, there's an issue with the `recheck_policy` call from `check` ÔÇö both calls return errors with the same shape (the policy error wrapped in `ToolDispatch`). Let me check: in the original code, when recheck_policy fails inside the hook Transform block (lines 856-877), the error is returned directly as `Err(e)`. When the L1 check fails in the main path (lines 947-985), the error is also returned directly as `Err(e)`. So in my CheckOutcome::Deny, I just wrap the error and create a synthetic audit. Good.

But wait, there's a subtle issue. In the original code, the `recheck_policy` is called twice in two different places:
1. Inside the hook Transform block (lines 856-877): if it fails, return immediately with the policy error and synthetic audit
2. In the main path (lines 947-985): if it fails, return immediately with the policy error and synthetic audit

In my refactor, the `check` method also calls `recheck_policy` once at the end. That's a behavior change ÔÇö instead of two separate call sites, there's one. But since the logic is the same, the behavior is preserved.

Wait ÔÇö is there any case where the recheck would behave differently? Let me think... The Transform branch calls recheck on `new_args`, then assigns `arguments = new_args`. After that, the main path also calls recheck on the (potentially new) `arguments`. So if the recheck inside Transform passes, the recheck in the main path also passes (since `arguments == new_args` now). So consolidating them is correct.

Actually, wait. There's a subtle issue. In the original code, after the hook Transform block, the recheck is done on `new_args`, then `arguments = new_args`. Then control flow falls through to the main path's recheck. So the main path recheck IS the same check on the same `new_args`. So yes, consolidating is fine.

Hmm, but there's still a subtle behavior difference. In the original code, if hook Transform returns and the policy check on `new_args` passes, then control falls through to the main path. In the main path, the recheck is done on the new `arguments` (which equals `new_args`). So the recheck is done twice on the same args ÔÇö once in the hook block, once in the main path. The second check is redundant but harmless.

In my refactor, the recheck is done once at the end of `check()`. This is functionally equivalent and slightly more efficient.

Now, let me also think about: do I want to call `recheck_policy` BEFORE the permission checks, AFTER them, or BOTH? In the original code:
- The static permission check (Phase 3) reads `check_static` which does NOT do the L1 policy check (it does the safety check, plan mode, bypass, dontask, acceptEdits, deny/allow rules, strict mode, but NOT the L1 shell/fs policy)
- The L1 policy check (Phase 7) is done separately in the main path, AFTER all permission checks

So the L1 policy check is a separate, post-permission phase. In my refactor, calling `recheck_policy` at the end of `check()` is correct.

But wait ÔÇö what about when `check_static` returns Denied? In the original code, when `check_static` returns Denied, the function returns immediately. The L1 policy check is NOT done. In my refactor, the L1 policy check would not be reached either (since we'd return early with `CheckOutcome::Deny`). Good.

OK, the design is sound. Let me also think about the safety_content extraction. In the original code, `safety_content_for_tool` is called BEFORE the permission check, and the result is passed to `check_static`. In my refactor, this is the same ÔÇö `safety_content` is computed at the start of `check()` and used in the static check.

One more consideration: the `safety_content_for_tool` function is defined in `mod.rs` at the bottom. I'll need to either:

use std::collections::HashMap;
use std::time::Instant;

/// Action a hook can request in response to an event.
#[derive(Debug, Clone)]
pub enum HookAction {
    /// Proceed normally.
    Continue,
    /// Skip this tool call (PreToolCall only; treated as Continue for other events).
    Skip,
    /// Abort with an error message (PreToolCall only; treated as Continue for other events).
    Error(String),
}

[step 21] -> Write {"contents":"//! Pre-execution permission pipeline for tool dispatch (Goal 261).\n//!\n//! Extracted from `ToolRegistry::invoke_with_audit` to make the\n//! permission-orchestration phases testable in isolation. The pipeline\n//! owns the seven pre-execution phases that decide whether a tool call\n//! is allowed to proceed and, if so, with what (possibly hook-transformed)\n//! arguments:\n//!\n//! 1. **Safety content extraction** ÔÇö derive the file-path \"content\" from\n//!    arguments so the static check can fire on protected paths (`.git`,\n//!    `.ssh`, etc.).\n//! 2. **Auto-mode LLM classifier** (Goal 200) ÔÇö for `PermissionMode::Auto`,\n//!    delegate the decision to the configured `AutoClassifier`.\n//! 3. **Static permission check** ÔÇö `LayeredPermissionsConfig::check_static`.\n//! 4. **Strict-mode handling** ÔÇö `Permission::Unknown` under Strict mode\n//!    becomes a `Denied`.\n//! 5. **Hook delegation** (Goal 212) ÔÇö for non-headless + interactive +\n//!    `Unknown` tools, call the registered `PermissionHook`. A `Transform`\n//!    result is re-checked against L1 policy before being accepted.\n//! 6. **Headless external hook** (Goal 199) ÔÇö for headless + interactive\n//!    tools, dispatch a `PermissionRequest` event to the external hook\n//!    runner.\n//! 7. **L1 policy check** ÔÇö shell/fs policies from the registry's\n//!    `PolicyConfig`. The same logic is exposed as `recheck_policy` for\n//!    re-validation of hook-mutated arguments.\n//!\n//! The pipeline borrows a `&ToolRegistry`; constructing one is cheap and\n//! does not perform any I/O. The expensive part is `check()`, which may\n//! await on the shared permissions lock, the auto-classifier, and (in\n//! headless mode) the external hook runner.\n\nuse serde_json::Value;\n\nuse crate::agent::PermissionDecision;\nuse crate::error::{Error, Result};\nuse crate::permissions::{DecisionReason, Permission, PermissionMode};\n\nuse super::policy_sandbox::PolicyConfig;\nuse super::{AuditMeta, ToolRegistry};\n\n// ÔöÇÔöÇ Outcome type ÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇ\n\n/// Result of a [`PermissionPipeline::check`] call.\n///\n/// - [`CheckOutcome::Deny`] ÔÇö the pipeline denied the call. The caller\n///   must surface `error` to the user and persist `audit` alongside it.\n/// - [`CheckOutcome::Allow`] ÔÇö the call is allowed. `arguments` is the\n///   final argument set (possibly hook-transformed) to pass to the tool.\n#[derive(Debug)]\npub enum CheckOutcome {\n    Deny {\n        error: Error,\n        audit: AuditMeta,\n    },\n    Allow {\n        arguments: Value,\n    },\n}\n\nimpl CheckOutcome {\n    /// Returns `true` if the pipeline denied the call.\n    pub fn is_deny(&self) -> bool {\n        matches!(self, CheckOutcome::Deny { .. })\n    }\n}\n\n// ÔöÇÔöÇ Pipeline type ÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇ\n\n/// Pre-execution permission pipeline. Borrows from a `ToolRegistry` so\n/// the orchestrating configuration (permissions, mode, hooks, policy,\n/// classifier, headless flag) stays in one place.\npub struct PermissionPipeline<'a> {\n    registry: &'a ToolRegistry,\n}\n\nimpl<'a> PermissionPipeline<'a> {\n    /// Construct a pipeline bound to `registry`. No I/O happens here.\n    pub fn new(registry: &'a ToolRegistry) -> Self {\n        Self { registry }\n    }\n\n    /// Run all pre-execution permission checks for `tool_name` with\n    /// `arguments`. Returns either a denial (with audit metadata) or the\n    /// (possibly hook-transformed) final arguments.\n    ///\n    /// This is a behavior-preserving extraction from\n    /// `ToolRegistry::invoke_with_audit`. The semantics of every code\n    /// path are unchanged.\n    pub async fn check(&self, tool_name: &str, mut arguments: Value) -> CheckOutcome {\n        // Phase 1: safety content (file-path content for protected-path check).\n        let safety_content = safety_content_for_tool(tool_name, &arguments);\n\n        // Phases 2-6: read shared permissions lock and run all permission checks.\n        if let Some(ref sp) = self.registry.permissions {\n            let guard = sp.read().await;\n\n            // Phase 2: Auto-mode LLM classifier (Goal 200).\n            if matches!(guard.mode, PermissionMode::Auto) {\n                if let Some(ref classifier) = self.registry.auto_classifier {\n                    let args_summary =\n                        serde_json::to_string(&arguments).unwrap_or_else(|_| \"{}\".into());\n                    let mut c = classifier.lock().await;\n                    match c.classify(tool_name, &args_summary, \"\").await {\n                        Ok((true, _reason)) => {\n                            if c.tracker.is_over_limit() {\n                                return CheckOutcome::Deny {\n                                    error: Error::PermissionDeniedLimit {\n                                        name: tool_name.into(),\n                                    },\n                                    audit: AuditMeta::synthetic_unknown_tool(tool_name),\n                                };\n                            }\n                            return CheckOutcome::Deny {\n                                error: Error::PermissionDenied {\n                                    name: tool_name.into(),\n                                    reason: DecisionReason::Mode(PermissionMode::Auto),\n                                },\n                                audit: AuditMeta::synthetic_unknown_tool(tool_name),\n                            };\n                        }\n                        Ok((false, _)) => {\n                            // Allowed by classifier ÔÇö fall through to static check.\n                        }\n                        Err(_e) => {\n                            // Classifier error ÔÇö conservative: allow static check to decide.\n                        }\n                    }\n                }\n                // If no classifier configured in Auto mode, fall through to static check.\n            }\n\n            // Phase 3: static permission check.\n            let is_readonly = self.registry.is_readonly(tool_name);\n            // Pre-compute interactive flag before the match so we can use it\n            // after without holding `guard` across an await point.\n            let is_interactive_tool = guard.any_interactive(tool_name);\n            let mut perm_is_unknown = false;\n            match guard.check_static(tool_name, is_readonly, safety_content.as_deref()) {\n                Permission::Denied(reason, _msg) => {\n                    return CheckOutcome::Deny {\n                        error: Error::PermissionDenied {\n                            name: tool_name.into(),\n                            reason: reason.clone(),\n                        },\n                        audit: AuditMeta::synthetic_unknown_tool(tool_name),\n                    };\n                }\n                Permission::Unknown => {\n                    perm_is_unknown = true;\n                }\n                Permission::Allowed(_) => {}\n            }\n\n            // Phase 4: Strict mode ÔÇö any tool without an explicit allow rule is denied.\n            if perm_is_unknown && matches!(guard.mode, PermissionMode::Strict) {\n                return CheckOutcome::Deny {\n                    error: Error::PermissionDenied {\n                        name: tool_name.into(),\n                        reason: DecisionReason::Mode(PermissionMode::Strict),\n                    },\n                    audit: AuditMeta::synthetic_unknown_tool(tool_name),\n                };\n            }\n\n            // Phase 5: hook delegation (non-headless + interactive + Unknown).\n            if perm_is_unknown && !self.registry.headless && is_interactive_tool {\n                if let Some(hook) = &self.registry.permission_hook {\n                    drop(guard);\n                    match hook.check(tool_name, &arguments).await {\n                        PermissionDecision::Deny(reason) => {\n                            return CheckOutcome::Deny {\n                                error: Error::PermissionDenied {\n                                    name: tool_name.into(),\n                                    reason: DecisionReason::Hook { name: reason },\n                                },\n                                audit: AuditMeta::synthetic_unknown_tool(tool_name),\n                            };\n                        }\n                        PermissionDecision::Transform(new_args) => {\n                            // Re-run policy check on the transformed arguments.\n                            // A malicious/compromised hook could use Transform\n                            // to substitute a different command/path that bypasses\n                            // the policy check already performed above.\n                            if let Err(e) = self.recheck_policy(tool_name, &new_args) {\n                                return CheckOutcome::Deny {\n                                    error: e,\n                                    audit: AuditMeta::synthetic_unknown_tool(tool_name),\n                                };\n                            }\n                            arguments = new_args;\n                        }\n                        PermissionDecision::Allow => {}\n                    }\n                    // Hook allowed/transformed; guard already dropped, skip headless block.\n                } else {\n                    // No hook registered ÔÇö non-headless library caller ÔåÆ allow.\n                    drop(guard);\n                }\n            } else if self.registry.headless && is_interactive_tool {\n                // Phase 6: headless mode ÔÇö interactive tools go through external hooks.\n                if self.registry.hook_runner.is_empty() {\n                    return CheckOutcome::Deny {\n                        error: Error::PermissionDenied {\n                            name: tool_name.into(),\n                            reason: DecisionReason::Hook {\n                                name: \"PermissionRequest\".into(),\n                            },\n                        },\n                        audit: AuditMeta::synthetic_unknown_tool(tool_name),\n                    };\n                }\n                let hook_input = crate::hooks::external::HookInput {\n                    event: crate::hooks::external::HookEvent::PermissionRequest,\n                    tool_name: Some(tool_name.to_string()),\n                    args: Some(arguments.clone()),\n                    mode: format!(\"{:?}\", self.registry.permission_mode),\n                    content: None,\n                    message: None,\n                    depth: None,\n                    reason: None,\n                    error: None,\n                };\n                // Drop the read guard before the async hook dispatch to\n                // avoid holding the lock across an await point.\n                drop(guard);\n                let hook_result = self.registry.hook_runner.dispatch(&hook_input).await;\n                if !matches!(hook_result.action, crate::hooks::HookAction::Continue) {\n                    return CheckOutcome::Deny {\n                        error: Error::PermissionDenied {\n                            name: tool_name.into(),\n                            reason: DecisionReason::Hook {\n                                name: \"PermissionRequest\".into(),\n                            },\n                        },\n                        audit: AuditMeta::synthetic_unknown_tool(tool_name),\n                    };\n                }\n            } else {\n                // Drop guard before tool execution (not holding across await).\n                if perm_is_unknown {\n                    // No explicit rule matched for this tool. It is being allowed\n                    // implicitly because the current permission mode is not Strict.\n                    // Consider using PermissionMode::Strict or adding an explicit\n                    // allow rule to silence this warning.\n                    tracing::warn!(\n                        tool = %tool_name,\n                        \"tool has no explicit permission rule; \\\n                         allowing implicitly (use strict mode to deny by default)\"\n                    );\n                }\n                drop(guard);\n            }\n        }\n\n        // Phase 7: L1 policy check (shell + fs). Same logic as the post-hook\n        // recheck; we run it here for the main path so a tool that passed\n        // permission checks is still subject to L1 policy.\n        if let Err(e) = self.recheck_policy(tool_name, &arguments) {\n            return CheckOutcome::Deny {\n                error: e,\n                audit: AuditMeta::synthetic_unknown_tool(tool_name),\n            };\n        }\n\n        CheckOutcome::Allow { arguments }\n    }\n\n    /// Re-run the L1 policy check on `arguments`. Used internally by\n    /// [`check`] when a hook returns [`PermissionDecision::Transform`]\n    /// (a malicious hook could mutate args to bypass the original policy\n    /// check), and exposed publicly so external callers can validate\n    /// hook-mutated arguments before re-dispatch.\n    ///\n    /// Behavior:\n    /// - If no L1 policy is configured on the registry, returns `Ok(())`.\n    /// - If `arguments[\"command\"]` is a string, runs `policy.check_shell(cmd)`.\n    /// - If `arguments[\"path\"]` or `arguments[\"file_path\"]` is a string,\n    ///   runs `policy.check_fs_path(path, is_write)`. `is_write` is\n    ///   `true` for `Write` / `Edit` / `StrReplace`, `false` otherwise.\n    ///\n    /// Returns the first policy error encountered. Callers must propagate\n    /// the error and stop dispatch.\n    pub fn recheck_policy(&self, tool_name: &str, arguments: &Value) -> Result<()> {\n        let Some(policy): Option<&PolicyConfig> = self.registry.policy.as_ref() else {\n            return Ok(());\n        };\n        if let Some(cmd) = arguments.get(\"command\").and_then(|v| v.as_str()) {\n            policy.check_shell(cmd)?;\n        }\n        let is_write = matches!(tool_name, \"Write\" | \"Edit\" | \"StrReplace\");\n        let path_arg = arguments\n            .get(\"path\")\n            .or_else(|| arguments.get(\"file_path\"))\n            .and_then(|v| v.as_str());\n        if let Some(path) = path_arg {\n            policy.check_fs_path(path, is_write)?;\n        }\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n// ÔöÇÔöÇ Helpers ÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇ\n\n/// Extract the file-path \"content\" from tool arguments for the safety\n/// check in `check_static`. Returns `None` for tools that don't operate\n/// on a file path.\n///\n/// - `Write` / `Read`: extract `args[\"path\"]`\n/// - `Edit`: extract `args[\"file_path\"]`\n/// - All other tools: `None`\nfn safety_content_for_tool(name: &str, args: &serde_json::Value) -> Option<String> {\n    match name {\n        \"Write\" | \"Read\" => args[\"path\"].as_str().map(String::from),\n        \"Edit\" => args[\"file_path\"].as_str().map(String::from),\n        _ => None,\n    }\n}\n\n// ÔöÇÔöÇ Tests ÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇ\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n    use crate::permissions::PermissionMode;\n    use crate::tools::policy_sandbox::{FsPolicy, ShellPolicy};\n    use async_trait::async_trait;\n\n    // ÔöÇÔöÇ recheck_policy tests (Goal 261 done-when) ÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇ\n\n    /// No policy configured ÔåÆ recheck_policy always returns Ok(()) even\n    /// if arguments contain policy-relevant fields.\n    #[test]\n    fn recheck_policy_with_no_policy_returns_ok() {\n        let registry = ToolRegistry::local();\n        let pipeline = PermissionPipeline::new(&registry);\n        let args = serde_json::json!({\n            \"command\": \"rm -rf /\",\n            \"path\": \"/etc/passwd\",\n        });\n        assert!(pipeline.recheck_policy(\"Bash\", &args).is_ok());\n    }\n\n    /// Policy configured, shell command doesn't match deny patterns ÔåÆ Ok.\n    #[test]\n    fn recheck_policy_allows_clean_shell_command() {\n        let policy = PolicyConfig {\n            shell: ShellPolicy {\n                deny_patterns: vec![\"rm -rf\".into()],\n            },\n            fs: FsPolicy::default(),\n        };\n        let registry = ToolRegistry::local().with_policy(policy);\n        let pipeline = PermissionPipeline::new(&registry);\n        let args = serde_json::json!({\"command\": \"ls -la\"});\n        assert!(pipeline.recheck_policy(\"Bash\", &args).is_ok());\n    }\n\n    /// Policy configured, shell command matches a deny pattern ÔåÆ Err.\n    #[test]\n    fn recheck_policy_blocks_denied_shell_command() {\n        let policy = PolicyConfig {\n            shell: ShellPolicy {\n                deny_patterns: vec![\"rm -rf\".into()],\n            },\n            fs: FsPolicy::default(),\n        };\n        let registry = ToolRegistry::local().with_policy(policy);\n        let pipeline = PermissionPipeline::new(&registry);\n        let args = serde_json::json!({\"command\": \"rm -rf /\"});\n        let err = pipeline.recheck_policy(\"Bash\", &args).unwrap_err();\n        assert!(matches!(err, Error::PermissionDenied { .. }));\n    }\n\n    /// Policy configured, file path doesn't match any deny prefix ÔåÆ Ok.\n    #[test]\n    fn recheck_policy_allows_clean_path() {\n        let policy = PolicyConfig {\n            shell: ShellPolicy::default(),\n            fs: FsPolicy {\n                deny: vec![\"/etc/\".into()],\n                ..Default::default()\n            },\n        };\n        let registry = ToolRegistry::local().with_policy(policy);\n        let pipeline = PermissionPipeline::new(&registry);\n        let args = serde_json::json!({\"path\": \"/tmp/scratch.txt\"});\n        assert!(pipeline.recheck_policy(\"Write\", &args).is_ok());\n    }\n\n    /// Policy configured, file path matches a deny prefix ÔåÆ Err.\n    #[test]\n    fn recheck_policy_blocks_denied_path() {\n        let policy = PolicyConfig {\n            shell: ShellPolicy::default(),\n            fs: FsPolicy {\n                deny: vec![\"/etc/\".into()],\n                ..Default::default()\n            },\n        };\n        let registry = ToolRegistry::local().with_policy(policy);\n        let pipeline = PermissionPipeline::new(&registry);\n        let args = serde_json::json!({\"path\": \"/etc/passwd\"});\n        let err = pipeline.recheck_policy(\"Write\", &args).unwrap_err();\n        assert!(matches!(err, Error::PermissionDenied { .. }));\n    }\n\n    /// Edit tool reads from `file_path` field, not `path`. A path passed\n    /// via `file_path` should still be subject to fs policy.\n    #[test]\n    fn recheck_policy_reads_file_path_for_edit_tool() {\n        let policy = PolicyConfig {\n ToolRegistry::local().with_policy(policy);\n        let pipeline = PermissionPipeline::new(&registry);\n        let args = serde_json::json!({\"file_path\": \"/secret/credentials\"});\n        let err = pipeline.recheck_policy(\"Edit\", &args).unwrap_err();\n        assert!(matches!(err, Error::PermissionDenied { .. }));\n    }\n\n    /// Read tool on a denied path: is_write=false, but the deny prefix\n    /// is checked regardless of read/write for fs policy.\n    #[test]\n    fn recheck_policy_read_tool_still_subject_to_fs_deny() {\n        let policy = PolicyConfig {\n            shell: ShellPolicy::default(),\n            fs: FsPolicy {\n                deny: vec![\"/secret/\".into()],\n                ..Default::default()\n            },\n        };\n        let registry = ToolRegistry::local().with_policy(policy);\n        let pipeline = PermissionPipeline::new(&registry);\n        let args = serde_json::json!({\"path\": \"/secret/file.txt\"});\n        // Read uses is_write=false; check_fs_path still checks the deny list\n        // before any allow-list logic (per policy_sandbox::check_fs_path).\n        let err = pipeline.recheck_policy(\"Read\", - `src/tools/mod.rs` (1608 lines) ÔÇö `ToolRegistry::invoke_with_audit` at lines ~675-895 is ~220 lines containing 7 pre-execution permission-check phases
- `src/permissions/mod.rs` ÔÇö `LayeredPermissionsConfig::check_static` returns `Permission::{Allowed,Denied,Unknown}`; `check_static` is the single source of truth for mode/rule resolution
- `src/hooks/external.rs` ÔÇö `HookAction::Continue` (line ~110), `ExternalHookRunner::is_empty`/`dispatch`, `HookInput` (line 74)

- `src/tools/policy_sandbox.rs` ÔÇö `PolicyConfig::check_shell` (line 99), `check_fs_path` (line 118) are the L1 policy methods

**Planned design (not yet committed):**
- New file `src/tools/permission_pipeline.rs`:
  - `pub struct PermissionPipeline<'a> { registry: &'a ToolRegistry }` ÔÇö borrow-based, no field duplication
  - `pub enum CheckOutcome { Deny { error: Error, audit: AuditMeta }, Allow { arguments: Value } }` with `is_deny()` helper
  - `new(registry)` constructor
  - `async fn check(name, arguments) -> CheckOutcome` ÔÇö extracts 7 phases: safety content extract ÔåÆ auto classifier ÔåÆ `check_static` ÔåÆ strict-mode deny ÔåÆ non-headless hook delegation (with Transform ÔåÆ recheck) ÔåÆ headless `ExternalHookRunner` dispatch ÔåÆ implicit-allow `tracing::warn!`
  - `fn recheck_policy(name, args) -> Result<(), Error>` ÔÇö re-runs `check_shell` + `check_fs_path`; used internally after hook `Transform` and exposed publicly
- Modify `src/tools/mod.rs`:
  - Add `pub mod permission_pipeline;`
  - `pub use permission_pipeline::{PermissionPipeline, CheckOutcome};`
  - `invoke_with_audit` shrinks to: pipeline.check call ÔåÆ touched_files record ÔåÆ tool lookup ÔåÆ side_effect/step_id/args_hash ÔåÆ tool.execute ÔåÆ audit construction

**Key decisions:**
- Lifetime-bound to `&ToolRegistry` (no field duplication, always current config)
- `recheck_policy` is one method serving both the original L1 check (after main check passes) and the post-`Transform` recheck (inside hook block)
- Keep L1 policy inside the pipeline (not in `invoke_with_audit`)

    /// Set the permissions configuration for this registry.
    pub fn with_permissions(mut self, permissions: PermissionsConfig) -> Self {
        self.permission_mode = permissions.mode.clone();
        self.permissions = Some(Arc::new(RwLock::new(permissions)));
        self
    }

/// - `Write` / `Read`: extract `args["path"]`
/// - `Edit`: extract `args["file_path"]`
/// - All other tools: `None`
fn safety_content_for_tool(name: &str, args: &serde_json::Value) -> Option<String> {
    match name {
        "Write" | "Read" => args["path"].as_str().map(String::from),
        "Edit" => args["file_path"].as_str().map(String::from),
        _ => None,
    }
}

// ÔöÇÔöÇ Goal-196: Safety path content extraction ÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇ

/// Extract the file-path "content" from tool arguments for the safety
/// check in `check_static`. Returns `None` for tools that don't operate
/// on a file path.
///
/// - `Write` / `Read`: extract `args["path"]`
/// - `Edit`: extract `args["file_path"]`
/// - All other tools: `None`
fn safety_content_for_tool(name: &str, args: &serde_json::Value) -> Option<String> {
    match name {
        "Write" | "Read" => args["path"].as_str().map(String::from),
        "Edit" => args["file_path"].as_str().map(String::from),
        _ => None,
    }
}

/// permission dialog. Extracts up to 80 characters.
pub fn args_preview_for_permission(arguments: &Value) -> String {
