                .iter()
                .take(3)
                .map(|(k, v)| {
                    let v_str = match v {
                        Value::String(s) => {
                            let short: String = s.chars().take(30).collect();
                            format!("\"{}\"", short)
                        }
                        other => {
                            let s = other.to_string();
                            s.chars().take(30).collect()
                        }
                    };
                    for

    #[tokio::test]
    async fn registry_dispatches_and_errors_on_unknown() {
        let reg = ToolRegistry::local().register(Arc::new(Echo));
        let out = reg
            .invoke("echo", serde_json::json!({"msg":"hi"}))
            .await
            .unwrap();
        assert_eq!(out, "hi");
        let err = reg.invoke("nope", serde_json::json!({})).await.unwrap_err();
        assert!(matches!(err, Error::UnknownTool(_)));
    }

    #[test]
    fn resolve_within_rejects_escape() {
        let root = std::path::Path::new("/work");
        assert!(resolve_within(root, "../etc/passwd").is_err());
        assert!(resolve_within(root, "/elsewhere").is_err());
        assert!(resolve_within(root, "src/lib.rs").is_ok());
    }

**Refactor delivered:**

1. **`PermissionPipeline` extraction** ÔÇö all 7 pre-execution phases (safety content ÔåÆ auto classifier ÔåÆ static check ÔåÆ strict mode ÔåÆ non-headless interactive hook w/ post-Transform recheck ÔåÆ headless external hook ÔåÆ L1 policy) moved out of `invoke_with_audit` and into `PermissionPipeline::check()`, returning a `CheckOutcome::Deny { error, audit } | Allow { arguments }` enum.

2. **`safety_content_for_tool` moved** to `permission_pipeline.rs` where it's actually called.

3. **`invoke_with_audit` is now 22 lines** ÔÇö pure delegation to the pipeline + dispatch to a new `dispatch_after_permission_check` helper that owns `touched_files` recording, tool lookup, `AuditMeta` construction, and `tool.execute()`.

4. **Public `PermissionPipeline::recheck_policy`** exposed as a standalone API for callers that need to re-validate hook-mutated arguments ÔÇö the two original `recheck_policy` call sites (post-hook Transform + main path) are now a single trailing call, behavior-equivalent because the Transform-branch recheck on `new_args` is identical to the main-path recheck on the now-assigned `arguments`.

5. **Two pre-existing `recheck_policy` sites collapsed into one** at the end of `check()` ÔÇö verified the consolidation is behavior-preserving by reading both branches.

6. **`Permission` import cleanup** ÔÇö removed from the production `use` line (now only used in `#[cfg(test)]`); no warnings.

**Refactor delivered:**

1. **`PermissionPipeline` extraction** ÔÇö all 7 pre-execution phases (safety content ÔåÆ auto classifier ÔåÆ static check ÔåÆ strict mode ÔåÆ non-headless interactive hook w/ post-Transform recheck ÔåÆ headless external hook ÔåÆ L1 policy) moved out of `invoke_with_audit` and into `PermissionPipeline::check()`, returning a `CheckOutcome::Deny { error, audit } | Allow { arguments }` enum.

2. **`safety_content_for_tool` moved** to `permission_pipeline.rs` where it's actually called.

3. **`invoke_with_audit` is now 22 lines** ÔÇö pure delegation to the pipeline + dispatch to a new `dispatch_after_permission_check` helper that owns `touched_files` recording, tool lookup, `AuditMeta` construction, and `tool.execute()`.

4. **Public `PermissionPipeline::recheck_policy`** exposed as a standalone API for callers that need to re-validate hook-mutated arguments ÔÇö the two original `recheck_policy` call sites (post-hook Transform + main path) are now a single trailing call, behavior-equivalent because the Transform-branch recheck on `new_args` is identical to the main-path recheck on the now-assigned `arguments`.

5. **Two pre-existing `recheck_policy` sites collapsed into one** at the end of `check()` ÔÇö verified the consolidation is behavior-preserving by reading both branches.

6. **`Permission` import cleanup** ÔÇö removed from the production `use` line (now only used in `#[cfg(test)]`); no warnings.
